<p><b>F.T. Island</b> (<a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>: <span lang="ko">에프티 아일랜드, or FT아일랜드</span>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: エフティー・アイランド; stylized as <b>FTISLAND</b>), also known as <b>Five Treasure Island</b>, is a five-member <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band formed by <a href="/wiki/FNC_Entertainment" title="FNC Entertainment">FNC Entertainment</a> in 2007. The band consists of <a href="/wiki/Choi_Jong-hoon" title="Choi Jong-hoon">Choi Jong-hoon</a> (leader, guitar, and keyboard), <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hong-gi" title="Lee Hong-gi">Lee Hong-gi</a> (main vocals), <a href="/wiki/Lee_Jae-jin_(musician,_born_1991)" title="Lee Jae-jin (musician, born 1991)">Lee Jae-jin</a> (bass and 2nd vocals), <a href="/wiki/Song_Seung-hyun" title="Song Seung-hyun">Song Seung-hyun</a> (guitar, vocals, and rap) replacing Oh Won-bin in 2009, and <a href="/wiki/Choi_Min-hwan" title="Choi Min-hwan">Choi Min-hwan</a> (drums and sub vocalist).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KBS_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-KBS-2">[2]</a></sup> On the other hand, F.T. Triple (A3), a sub-group of F.T. Island consisted of Jong-hoon, Jae-jin and Min-hwan, and has been inactive since 2012.</p>
<p>F.T. Island debuted in Korea on June 7, 2007, with the song, "Love Sick" on the music television program, <a href="/wiki/M_Countdown" title="M Countdown">M! Countdown</a>. The band's Korean debut was successful; their debut album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Cheerful_Sensibility" title="Cheerful Sensibility">Cheerful Sensibility</a></i> was the sixth best-selling album in 2007. Their debut song "Lovesick" topped the K-Pop charts for eight consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_Asia_-_F.T._Island_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Asia_-_F.T._Island-3">[3]</a></sup> Moreover, they also won the <a href="/wiki/Mnet_Asian_Music_Award_for_Best_New_Artist_(Solo_or_Group)" title="Mnet Asian Music Award for Best New Artist (Solo or Group)">Best New Male Group</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mnet_Asian_Music_Awards" title="Mnet Asian Music Awards">Mnet Asian Music Awards</a> and the Popularity and Newcomer Awards in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Disk_Awards" title="Golden Disk Awards">Golden Disk Awards</a> in 2007.</p>
<p>The band then debuted in Japan a year later, on June 8, 2008, with the EP, <i><a href="/wiki/Prologue_of_F.T._Island:_Soyogi" title="Prologue of F.T. Island: Soyogi">Prologue of F.T. Island: Soyogi</a></i>. However, it was met with limited success - it peaked at the 95th position in the Japanese charts and experienced sluggish album sales. It was not only until their third Japanese studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Five_Treasure_Island" title="Five Treasure Island">Five Treasure Island</a></i> with the title track "Flower Rock", which made them as successful artists in Japan. The album achieved 1st position in chart ranking sales and sold more than 45,000 copies in Japan. They are also the first Foreign Male Band to top the Oricon Daily Charts, which is the first band to top it in 42 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, F.T. Triple was formed and they released their first single "Love Letter" in the same year. The band then promoted the single on various music programmes in Korea. F.T. Triple has also performed in F.T. Island's concerts such as Men's Stories in 2010, and sang the OST "Don't You Know" for the drama <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Study" title="Master of Study">Master of Study</a>. Main vocalist Hong-gi made his solo debut in both Korea and Japan with a mini album and a full album respectively. The Korean album was titled as <i><a href="/wiki/FM302" title="FM302">FM302</a></i>, and the album was released on November 18, 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftisland-official.jp1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-ftisland-official.jp1-5">[5]</a></sup> while the Japanese album was titled as <i>AM302</i>, which was also released on December 9, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter.com_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>F.T. Island has released fifteen full-length albums, eight mini-albums, many singles and soundtrack productions for different drama theme songs and anime openings. F.T. Island is considered to be South Korea's first instrumental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K-pop_idol" title="K-pop idol">idol</a> band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korea_Herald_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Korea_Herald-7">[7]</a></sup> The band had also won various prestigious awards such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Disk_Awards" title="Golden Disk Awards">Golden Disk Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Music_Awards" title="Seoul Music Awards">Seoul Music Awards</a>, and held more than 10 different tours since debut.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007-08:_Debut_with_Cheerful_Sensibility_and_Japanese_Debut_with_Prologue_of_F.T._Island:_Soyogi">2007-08: Debut with <i>Cheerful Sensibility</i> and Japanese Debut with <i>Prologue of F.T. Island: Soyogi</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2007-08: Debut with Cheerful Sensibility and Japanese Debut with Prologue of F.T. Island: Soyogi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>F.T. Island's first album, <i><a href="/wiki/Cheerful_Sensibility" title="Cheerful Sensibility">Cheerful Sensibility</a></i>, was released on June 7, 2007. Prior to that, the members appeared on the Korean television show "Wanna be my girlfriend?" (<a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>: <span lang="ko">두근두근 여친만들기</span>) on <a href="/wiki/Mnet_(TV_channel)" title="Mnet (TV channel)">Mnet</a>. The band also performed live on stage at Rolling Hall and held their first official showcase at Live House Melon-AX, <a href="/wiki/Gwangjang-dong" title="Gwangjang-dong">Gwangjang-dong</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a> on May 27, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album combined 13 songs that were loosely divided into two parts, "<i>Emotional Chapter</i>" and "<i>F.T. Island Chapter</i>", which was according to the genre of the songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpopasia.com_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpopasia.com-9">[9]</a></sup> The "Emotional Chapter" consists of rock ballads, while the "F.T. Island Chapter" was produced by Japanese composers who worked with the Japanese band <i><a href="/wiki/SMAP" title="SMAP">SMAP</a></i>, who composed a variety of pop rock songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Selling over 79,000 copies in 2007, it was the sixth best-selling album of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YearEndCharts_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-YearEndCharts-11">[11]</a></sup> The album was later re-packaged on December 3, 2007, titled, <i>The Refreshment (Vol. 1.5)</i> with three extra songs, a photo book, a stack of photo cards and a mixing program called Music 2.0, which allows one to adjust the levels of the instruments and vocals. The edition sold 25,724 copies in December 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YearEndCharts_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-YearEndCharts-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FT_Island_from_acrofan_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="600" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/FT_Island_from_acrofan_%282%29.jpg/220px-FT_Island_from_acrofan_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/FT_Island_from_acrofan_%282%29.jpg/330px-FT_Island_from_acrofan_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/FT_Island_from_acrofan_%282%29.jpg/440px-FT_Island_from_acrofan_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FT_Island_from_acrofan_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
F.T. Island in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After debuting in Korea, FNC Entertainment (<i>formerly FNC Music</i>) moved F.T. Island's activities overseas. On March 31, 2008, an autograph session in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> at the Damansara Cineleisure was held, which was followed by the group's first concert at the Sunway Lagoon Amphitheater on the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> However, the performance was canceled,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> but was held in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> instead, at the <a href="/wiki/Siam_Paragon" title="Siam Paragon">Royal Paragon Hall</a> on April 14, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>F.T. Island's first Japanese debut album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Prologue_of_F.T._Island:_Soyogi" title="Prologue of F.T. Island: Soyogi">Prologue of F.T. Island: Soyogi</a></i>, was later released on June 7, 2008. The album consists of eight songs, two of which were newer versions of the original songs "F.T. Island" and "Primadonna". The last track, "Always Be Mine", is an English version of "First Kiss" from their debut album (though the lyrics are original). Music videos were also released for "Soyogi" and "Friendship", displaying the band's professionalism and playful sides.</p>
<p>After their promotional activities in Japan, the band then returned to Korea releasing their second Korean album <i><a href="/wiki/Colorful_Sensibility" title="Colorful Sensibility">Colorful Sensibility</a></i> on August 27, 2008. A follow-up epilogue, <i>Colorful Sensibility Part 2</i>, was later released on October 17.</p>
<p>Later that year, F.T. Island also released "The One", which was their first Japanese commercial single under an indie label AI Entertainment. The single charted at ninth on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> daily charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KTO_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-KTO-15">[15]</a></sup> The single was also the last official release with member Oh Won Bin before his departure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009-10:_Lineup_changes.2C_F.T._Triple_and_Breakthrough_in_Japan">2009-10: Lineup changes, F.T. Triple and Breakthrough in Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2009-10: Lineup changes, F.T. Triple and Breakthrough in Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 28, 2009, it was announced that member Oh Won Bin would indeed be leaving the group,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> with FNC trainee Song Seung-hyun replacing him as a guitarist and backup vocalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> With the new change in lineup, F.T. Island then released the music video for their mini-album with the title song, "Bad Woman".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> They also promoted it on <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Broadcasting_System" title="Seoul Broadcasting System">SBS</a> <a href="/wiki/Inkigayo" title="Inkigayo">Inkigayo</a>, and two days later, released the band's first Korean mini-album <i><a href="/wiki/Jump_Up_(EP)" title="Jump Up (EP)">Jump Up</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 22, F.T. Island later released their second Japanese single, "I Believe Myself".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> For the first time, members participated in lyrics composition. For the song "Moonlight Angel", member Jae-jin co-wrote the lyrics and leader Jong-hoon co-composed the song. "I Believe Myself" was the first Japanese single with member Seung-hyun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> They held their 2009 F.T. Island Tour-I Believe Myself in Osaka, Nagoya and Tokyo during the summer of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> F.T. Island also toured parts of Asia which included Singapore, Japan, Thailand, Taiwan, and others to promote themselves in the summer of 2009. The showcase kicked off in Singapore during June 25 to 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>While preparing for overseas promotions, the members were in the midst of recording their third album. On July 9, FNC Entertainment released jacket photos for the upcoming third album called <i><a href="/wiki/Cross_%26_Change" title="Cross &amp; Change">Cross &amp; Change</a></i>. On the following day, a music video teaser for "I Hope" was released online, featuring kids watching their idols (played by the members themselves) on TV. The title song, called “I Hope/Barae”, was released on July 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> F.T. Island tried out a variety of music styles for <i>Cross &amp; Change</i>; it included a total of 12 songs, ranging from moving ballads to addictive songs with a bright melody. F.T. Island adopted a new fashion style and concept for the album using a "retro" and the “Bokgo” approach, which was inspired during the “jeans jeans look” from the 80s in Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>F.T. Island released their 3rd Japanese single, "Raining", on October 21. A music video of the single was released. Leader Jong-hoon played the piano for the single for the first time instead of the guitar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>After celebrating their 1000th day in the music industry, they travelled to Japan and they stayed until the end of August to prepare for their major debut under their new Japanese label, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warner_Music" title="Warner Music">Warner Music</a> Japan. They also began a new Japanese television show which aired on April 7, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On May 19, F.T. Island released their new Japanese single "Flower Rock".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> It entered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oricon_chart" title="Oricon chart">oricon daily charts</a> in third position on May 19, 2010 on the day of its release, and held the fourth position of that week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> On July 14, F.T. Island released another single named "Brand-new days", which was written and composed by members Seung-hyun and Jong-hoon. F.T. Island performed a five-city concert tour in Japan after releasing both singles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> They also performed at the international rock festival <i>Summer Sonic 2010</i> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maishima_Arena" title="Maishima Arena">Maishima Arena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>After promotions in Japan, F.T. Island focused on their comeback in Korea in mid-August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Their new mini album <i><a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Journey" title="Beautiful Journey">Beautiful Journey</a></i> and the music video for their main title song "Love Love Love" were released on August 25. They held their comeback performance in Korea on August 27. The title song topped many popular music charts in South Korea and also gained international notice, especially in Taiwan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Jong-hoon co-wrote and co-composed the song, "Don Quixote's Song",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> making it their first Korean song that includes the composition of a member. In November and December, F.T. Island held performances such as the <i>Beautiful Journey Concert</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and <i>So Today... Concert</i> tour,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> in both Korea and Japan.</p>
<p>Whilst promoting their second Korean mini-album, F.T. Island recorded another Japanese single titled "<a href="/wiki/So_Today..." title="So Today...">So Today...</a>" that was released in November. The song, "Boom Boom Boom", was composed by Jong-hoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The single ranked sixth on the Oricon Daily Charts. With F.T. Island’s 3rd single taking the sixth position, they then had a record of all their singles ranking in the top ten of the Oricon charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> About 10,000 fans turned up at their promotional events in Osaka and Tokyo on 20 and 21 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The band then held a concert in Taiwan on December 25, celebrating Christmas together with 9000 fans. Former vocalist and guitarist Oh Wonbin, appeared as a special guest and performed his first single as a solo artist and a brand new song, which had not been released at the concert. F.T. Island performed songs in three languages, Korean, Japanese, and Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>With an album sales record of over 100,000, F.T. Island won favorable comments in the Taiwanese media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The revenue for concert tickets and merchandises alone and F.T. Island's <i>Beautiful Journey</i> concert had exceeded a total of NT$20Million.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They have been named the Korean artists who earned the most money in the end of 2010.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Four main news agencies namely, China Times, Yonhap News, Apple Daily and Liberty Times wrote news on the concerts, showing the band’s high popularity. F.T. Island also broke several records in Taiwan with 500,000 hits on mobile downloads and 10,000,000 hits on music downloads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011-12:_Continued_Japanese_popularity.2C_Return_to_Korea_and_rising_popularity">2011-12: Continued Japanese popularity, <i>Return</i> to Korea and rising popularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2011-12: Continued Japanese popularity, Return to Korea and rising popularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1993" data-file-width="3544" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg/220px-F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg/330px-F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg/440px-F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F.T._Island_Stand_Up_concert_20120309.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
F.T. Island performing during their Stand Up concert at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nokia_Theatre_L.A._Live" title="Nokia Theatre L.A. Live">Nokia Theatre L.A. Live</a>, March 9, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On April 20, 2011, F.T. Island released their seventh Japanese single "<a href="/wiki/Satisfaction_(F.T._Island_song)" title="Satisfaction (F.T. Island song)">Satisfaction</a>" with accompanying tracks, "Friends" and "I Want", in which Jong-hoon participated in the composition of both songs. The single debuted at number two on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> weekly singles charts, becoming the band's highest charting single in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OW_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-OW-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Their title song "Satisfaction" was also selected to be the ending theme song of <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Television" title="Fuji Television">Fuji Television</a>'s anime <a href="/wiki/Toriko" title="Toriko">Toriko</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 18, F.T. Island released their first major debut album in Japan, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Five_Treasure_Island" title="Five Treasure Island">Five Treasure Island</a></i>. The album features songs from their previous singles such as "Flower Rock", "Brand New Days", "So Today...", and "Satisfaction"; it also contains several new tracks, including the soundtracks for Japanese drama <i><a href="/wiki/Muscle_Girl!" title="Muscle Girl!">Muscle Girl!</a></i>, in which member Hong-gi played the lead male role. The album ranked first at the Oricon album daily chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late May, F.T. Island returned to the South Korean music scene after almost a year, with a mini-album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Return_(EP)" title="Return (EP)">Return</a></i>. The album was released on May 24. Title track was "Hello Hello", a fast-paced rock song. The album featured five songs in total. "I Confess" featured all of the members' vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korea_Herald_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Korea_Herald-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1817" data-file-width="3231" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg/220px-CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg/330px-CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg/440px-CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CN_Blue_and_F.T._Island_20120309.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
F.T. Island with <a href="/wiki/CNBLUE" title="CNBLUE">CNBLUE</a> during their Stand Up concert at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nokia_Theatre_L.A._Live" title="Nokia Theatre L.A. Live">Nokia Theatre L.A. Live</a>, March 9, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After releasing a tragic music video for their title track “Severely”, F.T. Island released their fourth mini-album, entitled <a href="/wiki/Grown-Up_(EP)" title="Grown-Up (EP)">Grown-Up</a>. Featuring five songs, it is composed of slow-tempo rock ballads. The album was released on January 31, 2012 and secured the No. 1 position on the Hanteo album chart for total album sales on both the daily and weekly charts, with title track "Severely" topping various online music charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The album was completely sold out ten days after its release, recording some 50,000 copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> F.T. Island also achieved the "Triple Crown" recognition for "Severely" on <a href="/wiki/JTBC" title="JTBC">JTBC</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_On_Top" title="Music On Top">Music On Top</a></i>. "Triple Crown" is a recognition for any artist who have won a music programme three times consecutively and the song would be removed from further trophies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 9, F.T. Island and fellow label-mates <a href="/wiki/CNBLUE" title="CNBLUE">CNBLUE</a> performed in America for the first time at Los Angeles <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nokia_Theatre_L.A._Live" title="Nokia Theatre L.A. Live">Nokia Theater</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April, the band returned to Japan to promote their 7th Japanese single "<a href="/wiki/Neverland_(song)" title="Neverland (song)">Neverland</a>", which was released on the 18th. “Neverland”, a fast tempo rock song, was chosen as the opening theme song of the animation Ozuma, a celebration of the 20th anniversary of Japanese broadcasting system WOWOW.</p>
<p>F.T. Island released their second stiudio Japanese album <i><a href="/wiki/20_(Twenty)" title="20 (Twenty)">20 [Twenty]</a></i> on May 16, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> It debuted at number four on the weekly <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> albums chart, selling 41,726 copies in its first week,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oricon_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oricon-56">[56]</a></sup> earning the band their best first-week sales in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The same year, F.T. Island released their fourth Korean studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Five_Treasure_Box" title="Five Treasure Box">Five Treasure Box</a></i> and its single "I Wish" on September 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Within the first week of its release, the album sold over 30,000 copies in South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013-14:_Japanese_album.2C_overseas_activities.2C_comeback_in_Korea.2C_individual_promotions">2013-14: Japanese album, overseas activities, comeback in Korea, individual promotions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2013-14: Japanese album, overseas activities, comeback in Korea, individual promotions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The band continued their TAKE FTISLAND tour which started the year before in Seoul, Korea and went to Taiwan in December 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and continued the tour in Shanghai and Beijing, China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soompi_2013_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soompi_2013-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 27, 2013, F.T. Island released their single, "You Are My Life" with 2 tracks, "Beat It" and "Come Into My Dream".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> All three songs ended up in the top 5 of Japanese music site Dwango's K-Pop weekly ringtone chart. Also, their M/V for "You Are My Life" took first on Chinese video site <a href="/wiki/YinYueTai" title="YinYueTai">YinYueTai</a>'s Korea chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later on April 9, the band's 2009 album <i>Jump Up</i> topped Taiwanese music charts for Korean and Japanese releases, with "Bad Woman" ranking first on the songs chart, as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The group released their Japanese album <i><a href="/wiki/Rated-FT" title="Rated-FT">Rated-FT</a></i> in June 2013, where members composed tracks such as "Time To", "Hold My Hand", "Black Chocolate" and "Orange Sky".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The album charted at third on Japan's <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> Daily Album Chart on the day it is released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>F.T. Island released their 11th Japanese single "Theory of Happiness" on July 24, 2013. It included two tracks composed by the members which were "Eyes On Me" and "Rainy Day" which both topped the Oricon Daily Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The band became the first Korean band to perform three years in a row on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuji_TV" title="Fuji TV">Fuji TV</a>'s "Mezamashi Live!" on July 28, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> F.T. Island also performed live at rock festival, Summer Sonic 2013 in Tokyo on August 10 and in Osaka on August 11 which was their second appearance at the festival, after 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The band also completed their first Japan arena tour of seven cities, titled <i>F.T. Island Arena Tour 2013 ~Freedom~</i>, drawing an audience of 100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>F.T. Island returned to Korea in late September 2013, and released their self-composed mini-album <i><a href="/wiki/Thanks_To" title="Thanks To">Thanks To</a></i>, dedicated to their fans and supporters. "Memory" and "Always With You" was composed by main singer Hong-gi, "Try Again" by Jong-hoon, and "Falling Star" by Jae-jin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> They held a two-day concert in Seoul on 28 and 29 September, in front of 6000 fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The concert was called "FTHX", combining the first initials of the band FT with THX (thanks).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> 'Memory' by Hong-gi ranked No.1 on the Taiwanese Omusic chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> "According to the Taiwanese G-MUSIC Chart, F.T. ISLAND’s 6th anniversary album ‘THANKS TO’ ranked the weekly chart No.1 recording 28.84% sales among Asian album sales."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their Japanese Zepp Tour started on October 1, 2013 in Tokyo, and later performed in Sapporo, Osaka, Fukuoka, Shizuoka and Nagoya, as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halloween_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-halloween-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>The band made their official Korean comeback with their fifth mini album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mood_(EP)" title="The Mood (EP)">The Mood</a></i> on November 18, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> It topped the weekly Hanteo chart<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> and Gaon chart;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and ranked first on the online HMV chart in Japan for pre-released sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FTISLAND_in_Paris,_La_Cigale,_7.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/FTISLAND_in_Paris%2C_La_Cigale%2C_7.JPG/220px-FTISLAND_in_Paris%2C_La_Cigale%2C_7.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/FTISLAND_in_Paris%2C_La_Cigale%2C_7.JPG/330px-FTISLAND_in_Paris%2C_La_Cigale%2C_7.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/FTISLAND_in_Paris%2C_La_Cigale%2C_7.JPG/440px-FTISLAND_in_Paris%2C_La_Cigale%2C_7.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<p>F.T. Island started 2014 with a concert in Shanghai which was part of their FTISLAND’s 6th-anniversary tour. The band released multiple albums and singles in Japan. <i><a href="/wiki/New_Page_(album)" title="New Page (album)">New Page</a></i> was released on May 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-81">[81]</a></sup> it sold an estimated 22,000 copies worldwide and charted at 3rd on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> Daily Charts and 6th on the Oricon Weekly Charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>A few months later, F.T. Island then released a second album, titled <i>Japan Best – All About</i> in October with the title track "Be Free".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-81">[81]</a></sup> It topped the Gaon physical album chart during October 5 and 11 periods, Tower Records Daily Pre-Order Charts and HMV Korean-Asia Daily Charts. It also achieved 8th position on the Gaon album chart for that month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The band then released a new single, "To The Light" in October, which consists of three fully composed tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> "Mitaiken Future"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> was released on March 16 and "Beautiful" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> on January 15. "Mitaken Future" was later included in the album <i>New Page</i>. "Beautiful" charted at 4th position in Oricon's Daily Singles chart on the day same day when the album was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>F.T. Island also held several tours and announced partnership with Taiwanese clothing brand, STAYREAL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> They were invited and performed in one of China's most biggest music festival - Zebra Music Festival; where the band sang songs such as "Flower Rock" and "Freedom". Its ticket sales were also long sold out before the festival even started proving F.T. Island's immense popularity in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Moreover, the band were also invited to perform in the Japanese MTV - Unplugged segment that only top artists could perform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Also, Hong-gi was also chosen to be the MC for M Countdown's 10th-anniversary special which proves the member's talent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The members also promoted themselves individually throughout 2014. Min-hwan was cast in a musical <i>Joseph and the Amazing Technicolour Dreamcoat</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Seung-hyun collaborated with comedian Song Eun-yi for <i>Two Song Place</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and starred in the film, <i>No One to Trust in the World</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Hong-gi resumed filming <i><a href="/wiki/Bride_of_the_Century" title="Bride of the Century">Bride of the Century</a></i> after his fall on an icy road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> He also starred in the drama, <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_Farmer_(TV_series)" title="Modern Farmer (TV series)">Modern Farmer</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and released his new accessory brand Skullhong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <i>Hongstargram</i> was also released as a travel book where he took pictures in his first solo tour in different countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Jong-hoon was later announced in a new upcoming drama “Heroes”, said to premiere in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> He also launched his first Art Expedition In Japan where he showcased his artworks to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Jae-jin starred in Fashion Killa alongside Hong-gi as a special guest<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and also sang the title song for Bride of the Century, where member Hong-gi was starring in the drama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015-present:_Success_with_first_fully_self-composed_album_and_pursuing_a_new_genre">2015-present: Success with first fully self-composed album and pursuing a new genre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2015-present: Success with first fully self-composed album and pursuing a new genre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>They started the year with their World Tour called <i>2015 FTISLAND [FTHX] Tour</i> which included concerts in France, Brazil, Chile, Mexico and two dates in the United States, one in New York and one in Los Angeles.</p>
<p>After a year and four months of hiatus in Korea following their mini album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mood_(EP)" title="The Mood (EP)">The Mood</a></i>, FNC Entertainment announced F.T. Island's first fully self-composed album, <i><a href="/wiki/I_Will_(F.T._Island_album)" title="I Will (F.T. Island album)">I Will</a></i> which was released on March 23. The music video of "To The Light" was pre-released on YouTube on March 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The album peaked at 7th on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a> World Albums Chart in the second week of April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The title song "Pray" was also rated 99.0 out of a 100,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soompi.com_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-soompi.com-107">[107]</a></sup> a near perfect score on Chinese Music Charts while "To The Light" was rated 85.97.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soompi.com_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-soompi.com-107">[107]</a></sup> <i>I Will</i> also performed well on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaon_Chart" title="Gaon Chart">Gaon Chart</a>, peaking 1st in physical album raking and 3rd on the Gaon Social Charts in the third week of March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> F.T. Island sold 31,000 copies of the album peaking in 7th position for the highest number of album copies sold in the entire month of March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> "Pray" was also a huge success in China as they were awarded the <i>Most Popular Band in Asia</i>, one of the three major awards in that event. The members could not attend the event, but gave a video recording to thank fans for receiving the award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> F.T. Island next tour was titled as <i>We Will</i> which was held in China, Japan, Taiwan and more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>After their Korean comeback, F.T. Island then returned to the Japanese market with a new fully composed album, <i><a href="/wiki/5.....Go" title="5.....Go">5.....Go</a></i> released on May 13. The title song of the album, "Primavera" is a collaboration with Japanese rock singer <a href="/wiki/Takahiro_Moriuchi" title="Takahiro Moriuchi">Takahiro Moriuchi</a> from <a href="/wiki/One_Ok_Rock" title="One Ok Rock">One Ok Rock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The official M/V was released on YouTube on April 18. "Primavera" is a rock ballad song which means "spring" in Latin. In the album, it contained 10 fully self-composed songs where "Fish" was included in the album as an acoustic version. The album was also separated into 4 different sets. The first set contained only the songs whereas the second contained miscellaneous such as the official music video; the last two sets contained different performances for their Summer Sonic concert last year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftisland-official.jp_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ftisland-official.jp-113">[113]</a></sup> F.T. Island also celebrated their 5th Japanese anniversary with various tours and sang songs from their new album. It was a major career breakthrough as it received many good international praises and both the Korean and Japanese album brought a huge impact to viewers around the world.</p>
<p>3 months later, F.T. Island continued to release new songs titled "Puppy", which was a Japanese single and was included in the new album. "Puppy" was recorded to be F.T. Island's 35th single since their debut. In this new album, there are 2 new songs and it has 4 different sets. The first set contained only the songs whereas the second contained an additional DVD concert which was from 2014; the third set contained additional fan meeting footages while the last includes behind the scenes and other miscellaneous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftisland-official.jp_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-ftisland-official.jp-113">[113]</a></sup> The official M/V was published on YouTube on August 16. The song was a new type of genre and it concentrated on the playful and humorous sides for each of the members. The music video was rather colourful and it was the first time where a foreigner was seen in F.T. Island's music videos. Upon release, the album immediately topped Japan's Music Chart which proves the quality of the album as well as the band's immense fan base in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The song also managed to claim the sixth position in Billboard's Japan Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> After "Puppy"'s success in Japan, F.T. Island then released the Korean version of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The band then held an autumn tour in 13 different countries within 32 days. The tour consisted of Nagoya, Osaka and Sendai, and many more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, it was announced that F.T. Island would have Korean and Japanese comebacks this year as well. The Japanese studio album is titled <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N.W.U_(album)" title="N.W.U (album)">N.W.U</a></i>. It is the acronym of 'Naite' (泣いて, to cry), 'Waratte' (笑って, to laugh), 'Utatte' (歌って, to sing) and was released on 6 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> All tracks in the album except the title song was composed and written by the members. The M/V for the song "You Don't Know Who I Am" was released on 18 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> 7 days later, the highlight medley was released on YouTube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Upon release, the album ranked first on the Japanese’s Tower Record, which is the largest record store in Japan, and second on the Oricon daily album chart. It also topped the HMV Asia daily charts and K-pop charts for famous Japanese sound sources such as Dwango.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> An Arena Tour was also held, titled LAW of FTISLAND: NWU. The tour was held in Osaka, Tokyo and Aichi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-122">[122]</a></sup> The tour was then extended to have another concert in Nippon Budokan Tokyo after gathering hot responses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 11, FNC Entertainment announced F.T. Island's sixth Korean studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Where%27s_the_Truth%3F" title="Where's the Truth?">Where's the Truth?</a></i> which was released on 18 July. The title song is titled as "Take Me Now" and it is a track personally produced by the members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The M/V was released on the same day in YouTube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> With the already success of their previous album <i>I Will</i>, <i>Where's the Truth?</i> managed to break its previous record by ranking in 5th position on Billboard's World Album Charts (<i>I Will</i> charted at 7th position). This was the band's first top 5 entry in this category and it was the best selling K-pop album in that week of its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The band still managed to maintain the top 10 position for the next week, at the ninth world's best selling album.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The album also charted at 1st in the Gaon Album Chart for the week of July 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In an interview with the band, the band was asked why they wanted to pursue rock genre again, in which Hong-gi answered, "We threw away what is popular. We showed you popular rock for the past 8 years. In our 9th year, we started to slowly show you the music that we want to do. Lately, it’s hard to find band music on music charts. We wanted to show how we changed based on the fame we earned through popular music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the same day as the release for the M/V for "Take Me Now", the band's 37th single "Just Do It" was also released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The single was also a huge success as well. It topped HMV's Asian album chart, Amazon Japan's Asian pop chart; landed in the top 3 on Tower Records' world music chart and hit No.5 on the Oricon Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> On September 2, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Japan" title="Universal Studios Japan">Universal Studios Japan</a> announced that F.T. Island is the first <a href="/wiki/K-pop" title="K-pop">k-pop</a> group to have a song that can be played in the ride "<a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Dream_%E2%80%93_The_Ride" title="Hollywood Dream – The Ride">Hollywood Dream</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The song also came atop in Tower Records Japan for the top 10 k-pop singles and albums for the second week of September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-unit">Sub-unit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sub-unit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2009, Jong-hoon, Min-hwan, and Jae-jin formed a sub-group called F.T. Triple. Some of the reasons behind this lineup were to showcase more of the members' skills and to prevent main singer, Lee Hong-gi, from overstraining his voice again. Another reason was to continue promoting F.T. Island while Hong-gi was filming <i><a href="/wiki/You%27re_Beautiful_(TV_series)" title="You're Beautiful (TV series)">You're Beautiful</a></i> while Seung-hyun was having a break.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KBS_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-KBS-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>At first, the trio was unofficially announced at the Dream Concert in Japan as "A3". They almost named themselves A3 because they all are of blood type 'A'. They also wanted to keep the F.T. name hence adding Triple at the end of it to represent a trio.</p>
<p>In F.T. triple, Jae-jin originally in charge of bass for F.T. Island becomes a guitarist and the main vocalist; Jong-hoon plays the piano and Min-hwan continues to play the drums. Their first single was titled "Love Letter" and was released with F.T. Island's 2CD Repackaged Album <i>Double Date</i> and a second CD named <i>Two Date</i> that features all of F.T. Triple's songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyric_writing_and_music_composition">Lyric writing and music composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lyric writing and music composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Every member of F.T. Island has been actively taking part in writing lyrics and composing music. The first member to participate in composing music was Jong-hoon, who co-wrote the song "돈키호테의 노래 (Don Quixote's Song)" in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The song was later included in the album <i><a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Journey" title="Beautiful Journey">Beautiful Journey</a></i>. He also composed the music for "고백합니다 (I Confess)" which was included in the EP <i><a href="/wiki/Return_(EP)" title="Return (EP)">Return</a></i> in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> as well as "We Hope to Become Lovers (애인이 돼 주길 바래요)" in the album <i><a href="/wiki/Grown-Up_(EP)" title="Grown-Up (EP)">Grown-up</a></i> in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the album <i><a href="/wiki/Five_Treasure_Box" title="Five Treasure Box">Five Treasure Box</a></i>, all members took part in either lyric-writing or composing music. Jong-hoon co-composed the song "U (All I Want Is You)" and wrote lyrics as well as composing music in "Let It Go!". Hong-gi took part in writing lyrics for "Stay With Me", "Life" and "Compass (The Way)", while Jae-jin composed the music and wrote the lyrics for "Paper Plane". Seung-hyun together with Min-hwan composed the music for "Wanna Go (World Does Not End Song)" as well as "Compass (The Way)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2015 album <i><a href="/wiki/I_Will_(F.T._Island_album)" title="I Will (F.T. Island album)">I Will</a></i>, all members except Min-hwan was active in lyric writing and music composition. For the first track of the album titled "Intro", Hong-gi composed the music. For the title track "Pray", Jong-hoon, Hong-gi, Jae-jin and Seung-hyun worked together to write the lyrics and Jong-hoon composed the music as well. Hong-gi took part in lyric writing as well as music composition for the third track "Black Chocolate". "BPM69"'s lyrics was written by Hong-gi and Jae-jin, Jae-jin also took part in co-composing the music as well. For the fifth track "Do You Know Why", Hong-gi wrote the lyrics while Jong-hoon composed the music. "Hey Girl" was written by Jong-hoon and Jae-jin, and Jong-hoon also took part in composing the music for that song. The next track "To The Light" was penned by Hong-gi and Jae-jin, with Jae-jin also composing the music. Their 8th track "Time to" was penned by Jae-jin as well as taking part in composing the music. "Shadow" was entirely written and composed by Jae-jin, while "Please" was written and composed by Jong-hoon. For the last track "Light", it was entirely penned and composed by Hong-gi himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the album <i><a href="/wiki/Where%27s_the_Truth%3F" title="Where's the Truth?">Where's the Truth?</a></i>, Hong-gi wrote the lyrics for "Out of Love", "Take Me Now", "Wonderful Life" and "We Are...". Jong-hoon wrote the lyrics for "가면(MASK)", "너에게 물들어(Becoming You)" and "Paparazzi" while Jae-jin penned the lyrics for "Lose" and "Stand By Me". For music composition, Jong-hoon composed "가면(MASK)", "너에게 물들어(Becoming You)" and "Paparazzi" while Jae-jin composed the music for "Lose", "너에게 물들어(Becoming You)" and "Stand By Me". Seung-hyun also composed the music for "Paparazzi".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=F.T._Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_F.T._Island" title="List of awards and nominations received by F.T. Island">List of awards and nominations received by F.T. Island</a></div>
<p>F.T. Island have won several major industry awards in South Korea, including several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Disk_Awards" title="Golden Disk Awards">Golden Disk Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mnet_Asian_Music_Awards" title="Mnet Asian Music Awards">Mnet Asian Music Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Music_Awards" title="Seoul Music Awards">Seoul Music Awards</a>. They have also topped popular television music program charts like <i><a href="/wiki/Inkigayo" title="Inkigayo">Inkigayo</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M!_Countdown" title="M! Countdown">M! Countdown</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Bank_(TV_series)" title="Music Bank (TV series)">Music Bank</a></i>.</p>
